Question #214 (ID: 505931)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 1st Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You are shortlisted for a scholarship that requires a written test and an interview. A friend asks you to prepare sample documents and a preparation plan to help them apply too. Produce adaptable templates and schedules.

Options:
ক. Write a brief email to your mentor summarizing your scholarship preparation and requesting feedback on your personal statement.
খ. Draft a compelling 150–200 word personal statement paragraph suitable for a scholarship form.
গ. Design a three-week mock-test schedule (what tests to take each week and focus areas).
ঘ. List five common scholarship interview questions and a concise model answer for each.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
ক
Subject: Request for Feedback on My Scholarship Preparation and Personal Statement

Dear [Mentor’s Name],

I hope you are doing well. I have been preparing for the [Scholarship Name] by revising the syllabus, completing timed practice tests, and compiling evidence of extracurricular achievements. I have attached my draft personal statement and a one-page summary of relevant projects and volunteer work.

Could you please review my personal statement for clarity and impact? I would appreciate suggestions on tone, emphasis of achievements, and any gaps you notice. If possible, could we meet for 20–30 minutes this week for quick feedback?

Thank you for your guidance — it would mean a lot as I finalise my application.

Warm regards,
[Your Name]

খ
Personal Statement (150–200 words):

I am applying for the [Scholarship Name] because I believe education is the most reliable pathway to create positive change in my community. Throughout school, I have balanced academic excellence with leadership: I headed the science club, organised neighborhood tutoring for younger students, and led a small research project on water purification techniques. These experiences taught me project management, teamwork, and the value of translating ideas into action. Academically, I have consistently achieved high grades in STEM subjects and pursued additional online courses to deepen my understanding. With this scholarship, I aim to pursue [degree field] so I can develop practical solutions to public health challenges in rural areas. I am committed to using the opportunities this scholarship provides to both excel academically and pay forward the support through outreach and mentorship programs.

গ
Three-Week Mock-Test Schedule:
Week 1 — Diagnostic and Foundation:
- Day 1: Full-length diagnostic test (timed) to identify weaknesses.
- Days 2–6: Daily focused practice on weakest two areas (45–60 minutes each), short daily quizzes.
- Day 7: Mini-mock (half paper) to measure progress.

Week 2 — Skill-Building and Timing:
- Day 1: Full timed practice test focusing on time allocation.
- Days 2–5: Practice medium-difficulty question banks, 1–2 timed sections per day.
- Day 6: Peer-review session: swap answers and discuss reasoning.
- Day 7: Full mock test under exam conditions.

Week 3 — Polishing and Interview Prep:
- Day 1: Full mock test; evening: in-depth review of errors.
- Days 2–4: Short daily mocks (2 sections) plus polishing personal statement and achievements list.
- Day 5: Mock interview with friend/mentor (record if possible).
- Day 6: Light practice and rest; compile quick-reference notes.
- Day 7: Rest and mental preparation; final checklist for documents.

ঘ
Five Common Scholarship Interview Questions and Model Answers:
1) Why do you deserve this scholarship?
Model answer: I believe I combine academic dedication with community impact; my grades show commitment while my tutoring program demonstrates a desire to help others. With this scholarship I can access education that will amplify my ability to solve local problems.

2) Tell us about a challenge you overcame.
Model answer: During a community project, we lacked funding and resources. I led fundraising and partnered with a local NGO to secure materials, reorganised tasks to match volunteer skills, and completed the project on time — teaching me adaptability and leadership.

3) What are your long-term goals?
Model answer: I plan to complete a degree in [field], specialise in [specific area], and work on scalable projects that improve public services in underserved regions. I also want to mentor future students from my community.

4) How will you use this scholarship if awarded?
Model answer: I will use it to cover tuition and essential learning materials, and invest time in research projects and community internships that develop practical skills aligned with my goals.

5) Describe a teamwork experience and your role.
Model answer: In a science fair project, I was the coordinator: I organised meetings, divided tasks based on strengths, and mediated disagreements. We completed the project successfully and won recognition — showing my planning and communication skills.


Explanation:
The mentor email (ক) is concise, shows preparedness, and requests specific, time-limited feedback, which mentors appreciate. The personal statement (খ) highlights academic achievement, leadership, community impact, and future intent — the core elements selection committees seek. The three-week mock-test schedule (গ) progresses from diagnostic to timed practice and interview readiness, balancing intensity with recovery. The interview Q&A (ঘ) gives brief, transferable model answers: each focuses on evidence (what you did), the skills developed, and the broader impact or plan — the structure interviewers find convincing.

Question #215 (ID: 505851)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 1st Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
While returning from school, a class five boy discovered a leather wallet lying under a bench in the park. Inside there were several notes, a driver's licence with the owner's name and address, and a small shopping list. The boy thought about taking the money because his family needed groceries, but he decided to act. He walked to the nearest community center for help.

Options:
ক. এই পরিস্থিতিতে ছেলেটির প্রথম করণীয় কী হওয়া উচিত?
খ. কমিউনিটি সেন্টারের কার কাছে বা কীভাবে তাকে হস্তান্তর করা উচিত?
গ. যদি মালিক শনাক্ত হয়, তাঁর সম্ভাব্য প্রতিক্রিয়া এবং কীভাবে ছেলেটিকে পুরস্কৃত বা ধন্যবাদ জানানো যেতে পারে?
ঘ. এই ঘটনাতে কী নৈতিক শিক্ষা নেওয়া যায় এবং ভবিষ্যতে একই সিদ্ধান্তের সুফল কী হতে পারে?


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
ক উত্তর: ছেলেটির প্রথম করণীয় হওয়া উচিত নিরাপদভাবে ও শালীনভাবে প্যার্সটি ধরে রাখা এবং দ্রুতই নির্ভরযোগ্য প্রাপ্তিকে জানানো — যেমন স্কুলের শিক্ষক, কমিউনিটি সেন্টার অথবা নিকটস্থ পুলিশ স্টেশন। সে প্যার্সটি নিজের কাছে না রেখে অনেকে দেখার জায়গায় রেখে বা একজন বড় বা কর্মকর্তা কে দিলেই ঠিক। এটি মুদ্রা উধাও বা ভুল সিদ্ধান্ত নেওয়া প্রতিরোধ করবে।

খ উত্তর: পার্সটি কমিউনিটি সেন্টারের রিসেপশনে বা দায়িত্বশিল্পী (যদি সেখানে নিরাপত্তা বা চেয়ারের দায়িত্বে কেউ থাকে) এবং পরে পুলিশে বা মালিককে সরাসরি হস্তান্তর করা উচিত। রেকর্ড রাখার জন্য একটি ছোট নোট বা রিসিট তৈরি করা উচিত: পেয়ে থাকবার সময়, যে ব্যক্তি পেয়েছে, এবং যাকে হস্তান্তর করা হলো—এগুলো লিখে রাখা ভালো। যদি মালিকের ঠিকানা রয়েছে, প্রথমে ফোন করে মিটিং ঠিক করা যেতে পারে, বা পুলিশ মাধ্যমে দেওয়ার পর মালিককে জানানো যেতে পারে।

গ উত্তর: মালিক যদি শনাক্ত হন, তিনি প্রথমে রিলিফ ও কৃতজ্ঞতা প্রকাশ করবেন; সম্ভবত তিনি ছেলেটিকে ধন্যবাদ জানাবেন, এবং প্রয়োজনে পুরস্কার বা উপহার দিতে পারেন। পুরস্কার নিলে ছেলেটিকে বিনীতভাবে গ্রহণ করতে হবে এবং মালিককে বলতেই হবে যে সে ঠিক কাজ করেছিল। সমাজে এমন সততা উদাহরণ হিসেবে তুলে ধরা যেতে পারে—বিদ্যালয় বা স্থানীয় সংবাদে ছোটখাটো ভূয়সী প্রশংসা বা স্কুল থেকে স্বীকৃতি মিলতে পারে।

ঘ উত্তর: নৈতিক শিক্ষা: 'সত্যনিষ্ঠা ও দায়িত্বশীলতা'—অতিরিক্ত অর্থে ক্লান্তি আসলেও সঠিক কাজ করা শেষ পর্যন্ত বড় সুবিধা আনে। ভবিষ্যতে এই ধরনের সিদ্ধান্ত শিশুটিকে বিশ্বাসযোগ্য, সম্মানিত ও শান্তিপূর্ণ নাগরিক হিসেবে গড়ে তুলবে; পাশাপাশি সামাজিক সম্পর্ক ও সম্মান বাড়বে।

Explanation:
এই পরিস্থিতি বিশ্লেষণ করলে দেখা যায়—কারও নিখুঁত হতে পারে তাত্ক্ষণিক লাভের প্রলোভন, কিন্তু দীর্ঘমেয়াদি নৈতিক ও সামাজিক ফলাফল গুরুত্বপূর্ণ। প্রথমে নিস্তেজ না হয়ে দায়িত্বশীল বড়দের জানানোর কারণ: ১) অনুমানহীন সিদ্ধান্ত (যেমন নিজের রাখা) আইনি ও নৈতিক সমস্যা সৃষ্টি করতে পারে; ২) পুলিশ/কমিউনিটি সেন্টারের মাধ্যমে ফেরত দিলে মালিক দ্রুত ও নিরাপদে পাবে; ৩) রেকর্ড বজায় রাখলে ভুল বোঝাবুঝি এড়ানো যায়। মালিকের কৃতজ্ঞতা ও সম্ভাব্য পুরস্কার হল প্রতীকী—মতো করে বলা যায় এই ধরনের আচরণ সমাজে অনুকরণীয় হিসেবে দেখা হয়। মোটকথা, ছোট বেলায় গৃহীত সততা বড় চরিত্রকে গড়ে তোলে।

Question #216 (ID: 505803)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 1st Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You received a concerned message from your father saying he noticed you've been working a part-time job while preparing for the HSC exams and he is worried that the job will affect your results. Prepare responses that reassure him and show a clear plan.

Options:
ক. Write an email reply to your father reassuring him and explaining your situation.
খ. Provide a two-week study timetable that balances work and study (give days, times, subjects/tasks).
গ. Explain three specific strategies you will use to make sure the part-time job does not harm your exam preparation.
ঘ. Write a short closing paragraph asking for your father's support and understanding.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
ক
Dear Baba,

Thank you for being so thoughtful about my future — I understand your concern. I want to reassure you that I am fully committed to my HSC preparation. I accepted the part-time job to help with some family expenses and to gain time-management experience, but I have arranged my schedule so that study remains my top priority.

I have a clear study plan, I attend all classes, and I use weekends and evenings for focused revision. I am also taking regular mock tests and reviewing my mistakes with teachers. If ever you feel my grades are slipping, please tell me — I welcome your guidance.

Please be assured: I will not let the job interfere with my exam goals.

With love,
[Your Name]

খ
Two-week combined work-study timetable (sample):
Week 1
- Monday: 6:00–8:00 AM — Mathematics (problem practice)
          8:30 AM–12:30 PM — College/classes
          2:00–6:00 PM — Part-time job (Mon, Wed, Fri)
          8:00–10:00 PM — Chemistry (notes & past paper)
- Tuesday: 6:00–8:00 AM — English (reading & writing)
           8:30 AM–12:30 PM — College
           4:00–7:00 PM — Self-study: Biology (diagrams)
           8:00–10:00 PM — Revision: weak topics
- Wednesday: same as Monday
- Thursday: 6:00–9:00 PM — Extra study session (no job)
- Friday: same as Monday
- Saturday: 9:00 AM–1:00 PM — Mock test / timed practice
            3:00–6:00 PM — Review mock answers
            8:00–10:00 PM — Light revision & rest
- Sunday: 9:00 AM–12:00 PM — Consolidation & notes
          Afternoon — rest / family time
Week 2
- Keep the same morning routine; swap subjects so each subject gets at least two focused sessions per week. Reserve weekend for longer practice tests and topic revision. Limit work shifts to 12–15 hours per week maximum so evenings and mornings remain for study.

গ
Three strategies to prevent job interfering with study:
1) Strict time boundaries: Fix fixed hours for the job (e.g., late afternoon only) and protect morning best-study hours and two evening hours for focused revision. No overtime during exam months.
2) Prioritize tasks and use focused study techniques: Use Pomodoro (25–45 min study blocks with short breaks), active recall, and past papers to gain maximum learning in limited time.
3) Regular monitoring and flexibility: Weekly self-assessment (quick quizzes or mock sections) to spot falling performance; if marks drop or fatigue increases, reduce work hours immediately and reallocate time to study.

ঘ
Closing paragraph:
I know you want the best for me, and I appreciate your care. Please trust my plan for a few weeks — if the balance doesn't work I will stop the job. Your support and occasional check-ins mean a lot to me. Thank you for believing in me.

With affection,
[Your Name]

Explanation:
This solution combines reassurance (personal message), a concrete timetable (so the father can see study hours are protected), practical strategies (time boundaries, effective study methods, monitoring), and a respectful closing asking for support. Including a sample timetable demonstrates realistic time management, while the strategies focus on maximizing learning efficiency and ensuring flexibility so work can be reduced if needed.

Question #217 (ID: 505804)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 1st Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Your elder sister messaged you after seeing your recent low scores in mock exams; she fears you might fail the HSC. You need to respond, accept responsibility where appropriate, and present a clear recovery plan to regain her confidence.

Options:
ক. Write a calm, honest reply to your sister explaining the reasons for the low mock scores and acknowledging any mistakes.
খ. List five concrete actions you will take in the next month to improve your marks (include study methods and resources).
গ. Draft a short weekly checkpoint message you will send your sister to keep her informed of progress.
ঘ. Write one paragraph explaining how you'll manage stress and stay motivated during this improvement period.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
ক
Dear Didi,

Thank you for caring — I know the mock results were disappointing. I want to be honest: I underestimated the exam format and spent too much time on easier topics while neglecting tougher ones. I also allowed distractions (phone/social apps) to cut into study time. I take full responsibility and I'm ready to work harder.

Please don't worry; I have a recovery plan and I want your support.

Love,
[Your Name]

খ
Five actions for the next month:
1) Topic gap analysis: Spend two days identifying weakest chapters from each subject using the mock answer scripts.
2) Focus blocks: Daily 90-minute focused sessions for each weak subject using active recall and spaced repetition.
3) Past papers: Complete one full past-paper twice weekly under timed conditions; review mistakes immediately and log them.
4) Extra help: Attend one additional tutoring session per week for the two weakest subjects and form a weekly study group with classmates for peer teaching.
5) Resource optimization: Use specific resources — standard textbooks for theory, past HSC solution collections, online video lessons for difficult concepts, and concise flashcards for last-minute revision.

গ
Weekly checkpoint message (example to send every Sunday evening):
"Didi, weekly update: Completed 3 timed past-paper sections, improved average score in Biology from 55% to 68% in chapter tests, attended two extra tutoring sessions, and revised chapters 4–6 in Math. Plan for next week: full Math past paper and two Chemistry focused sessions. Feeling more confident. Love, [Your Name]."

ঘ
Managing stress and motivation:
I will build short daily routines that include 30 minutes of light exercise and 10 minutes of mindfulness to reduce anxiety. I will set small measurable goals (e.g., increase chapter test score by 10% per week) and celebrate small wins. Regular sleep, short breaks during study (Pomodoro), and keeping in touch with you for encouragement will help me stay motivated and avoid burnout.

Explanation:
This solution is honest about causes, provides a practical recovery plan with measurable steps, and sets up accountability by promising weekly updates. The five actions combine diagnosis, focused study, practice, external help, and resource use. The checkpoint message is concise and informative, giving the sister confidence through measurable improvements. Stress-management techniques are practical and evidence-based (exercise, sleep, small wins) to keep motivation steady.

Question #218 (ID: 505805)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 1st Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Your HSC teacher emailed expressing concern because you missed several classes due to illness and asked you to explain how you will catch up and request any necessary accommodations. Prepare a professional reply and a catch-up plan.

Options:
ক. Write a polite email reply to the teacher explaining your absence and expressing willingness to catch up.
খ. Provide a detailed 3-week catch-up plan listing topics, study activities, and deadlines.
গ. State two reasonable accommodations you might request from the teacher (e.g., deadline extension, extra marking), and justify each.
ঘ. Explain how you will ensure you do not fall behind again (two preventive measures).


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
ক
Subject: Catching up after recent illness

Dear Sir/Madam,

Thank you for your concern. I was unwell for five days with a high fever and followed the doctor's advice to rest. I apologize for missing your classes. I am committed to making up for the lost time and would appreciate any guidance or materials you recommend.

Below I have outlined a three-week catch-up plan and I would be grateful if you could confirm whether I should prioritize any particular topics or if there are handouts I missed. If possible, I would appreciate a short meeting (or emailed feedback) after I complete the plan.

Sincerely,
[Your Name]

খ
Three-week catch-up plan:
Week 1 (Topics A & B — foundational):
- Day 1: Obtain class notes and handouts; list all missed topics.
- Day 2: Read textbook sections for Topic A; create summary notes and concept maps.
- Day 3: Watch recommended lecture/video on Topic A; solve 10 practice problems.
- Day 4: Topic B reading and summary.
- Day 5: Attempt past paper questions related to A & B; mark and list mistakes.
- Weekend: Meet a classmate or tutor for 1-hour discussion to clarify doubts.
Week 2 (Topic C & D — application):
- Days 1–3: Deep study of Topic C with solved examples; do timed practice set.
- Days 4–5: Topic D focused study and group discussion.
- Weekend: Complete a mixed practice test covering A–D; send answers to teacher if requested.
Week 3 (Revision & assessment):
- Day 1: Review all summaries and flashcards for weak points.
- Day 2: Take another timed past-paper and self-assess.
- Day 3: Meet teacher for feedback (or email scanned answers) and correct errors.
- Remaining days: Final consolidation and plan for upcoming classes.
Deadlines: Finish Week 1 topics by end of first full week after recovery; Week 2 by the end of the second week; Week 3 consolidation finished before next major test.

গ
Two reasonable accommodations and justification:
1) Short deadline extensions for assignments due during the illness period: Justification — missed classes prevented me from receiving in-class explanations; a short extension (3–5 days) will allow submission of higher-quality work and demonstrate true understanding.
2) Opportunity for brief remedial feedback session (10–15 minutes) or the option to send solutions by email for review: Justification — targeted feedback will correct misunderstandings early and prevent repeated errors, helping me catch up faster and not burden future classes.

ঘ
Two preventive measures to avoid falling behind again:
1) Early communication: If I become ill or foresee absence, I will inform you promptly and request class notes so I can study immediately.
2) Build a short buffer: Maintain concise personal notes and recordings (where allowed) for each class so I can review the day’s lesson quickly if absent. Also arrange one weekly 30-minute peer-review with a classmate to stay aligned with class progress.

Explanation:
The email is polite and professional, acknowledges responsibility, and asks for teacher guidance. The catch-up plan breaks topics into manageable weekly goals with concrete activities (reading, videos, practice, peer discussion) and deadlines to show commitment. The accommodations requested are reasonable and justified by the disruption caused by illness. Preventive steps emphasize communication and small systems (notes/peer-review) that reduce the chance of falling behind in the future.

Kind regards,
[Your Name]


Explanation:
These emails cover key pre-arrival concerns: visa documentation and COE issuance process, mandatory health insurance and vaccinations, accommodation logistics including deposits and guarantors, and arrival-week services such as airport pickup and orientation. Each message uses a clear subject, numbered questions, and polite closings to make it easy for university staff to respond precisely. When communicating with ISS, include application or offer reference numbers and attach any requested documents to speed up processing.

খ. Write a short instant message (2–3 lines) you can send immediately.
গ. List three brief reasons (one line each) why this victory matters beyond the trophy.
ঘ. Suggest two practical ways you can help your friend prepare for the international forum (one academic/practice-related, one logistical/emotional).


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
ক
Subject: Huge Congratulations — National Champion and Best Wishes for the International Forum!

Dear [Friend's Name],

I was thrilled to hear you won first prize at the national debate — what an outstanding achievement! Your clarity of thought, sharp rebuttals and calm presence under pressure truly set you apart on stage.

ক. Compose a formal congratulatory email to your colleague from the debate club president (subject + 3 short paragraphs).
খ. Write a concise 3–4 line congratulatory blurb suitable for the department newsletter.
গ. Create a five-point preparation checklist your colleague can follow before the guest talk (bullet-style, actionable items).
ঘ. Propose two meaningful ways the department can honour the winner (one event-based, one permanent/record-based).


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
ক
Subject: Congratulations on Your Inter-University Victory

Dear [Colleague's Name],

On behalf of the Debate Club, congratulations on securing first prize at the inter-university debate. Your analytical rigor and poised delivery have brought great distinction to our university.

We appreciate the dedication you showed in research and teamwork; your success reflects the high standards of our club. We look forward to your upcoming guest talk and the insights you will share with students.

খ

গ

Solution:
ক Discover the Sundarbans: Mangroves, Tigers, and Tranquility

খ The Sundarbans—our vast, UNESCO-listed mangrove frontier—is a living classroom for conservation and calm. Join a small, eco-conscious group to explore tidal creeks and support local communities while minimizing your footprint.

গ Glide through a maze of winding waterways framed by dense mangroves where kingfishers and spotted deer appear at the water’s edge. With luck and patient watching, you may glimpse the elusive Royal Bengal Tiger or see otters playing at dusk; boats threaded along quiet channels reveal heron rookeries, crab-rich mudflats, and fishermen launching small nets against the amber light. The landscape shifts with tides—an ever-changing tapestry of green, brown, and mirrored sky.

ঘ Ready to book a responsible weekend adventure? Reply to this email or call +88-XXX-XXXXXXX to reserve your spot and receive a detailed eco-itinerary.

The closing (ঘ) includes a clear call-to-action and a contact prompt so the recipient knows how to proceed; it emphasizes responsible travel to align with the eco-friendly theme.

Question #227 (ID: 505667)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 1st Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You are Maya writing a short travel blog post about a sunrise river cruise on the Padma River. Prepare a title, the first paragraph, five photo captions, and three practical travel tips for readers.

Options:
ক. Write a catchy blog title (up to 7 words).
খ. Write the first paragraph (about 50–70 words) that paints the scene of the sunrise cruise.
গ. Provide five short photo captions suitable for images taken during the cruise.
ঘ. List three practical travel tips for readers planning the cruise (one sentence each).


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
ক Morning Light on the Padma

খ Before dawn the river is a sheet of quiet glass; as the sun lifts, mist peels from the water and fishermen’s boats become silhouettes against gold. Egrets launch like white flags, and children on the riverbank wave as our boat slips by, carrying the hush and slow rhythm of river life into the warming day.

গ 1. Dawn breaks over the Padma—gold on glass.
2. Fishermen haul in nets as the first light catches the ropes.
3. Riverbank tea stalls steam and wake the village.
4. A lone egret watches the current with patient grace.
5. Children race along the shore, laughter echoing across water.

ঘ 1. Bring a light waterproof jacket and a scarf—the morning mist is cool and damp.
2. Carry a small pair of binoculars and a telephoto lens for wildlife and candid river scenes.
3. Confirm tide and departure times with your operator; low or high tides change the route and landing spots.

Explanation:
The title (ক) is short, evocative, and optimized for a travel blog. The opening paragraph (খ) uses sensory language—visual (gold, silhouettes), auditory (laughter), and motion (boat slipping by)—to immerse readers in the experience and keep the word count in the requested range. The captions (গ) are concise and image-focused, each pairing a visual moment with a short phrase appropriate for social posts or a photo gallery. The travel tips (ঘ) are practical: clothing for mist, equipment for photographing wildlife and scenes, and logistical advice about tides and schedules—key considerations for a safe and satisfying river cruise.
